If it persists for several days, there is no harm. Once the protective qi becomes stronger, sweating will naturally stop, and there is nothing to worry about. However, for other mixed symptoms not caused by external pathogens that result in spontaneous or night sweats, treatment is necessary and should not be neglected.[51p]

    　　　　　战汗

    　　战与栗异，战由乎外，栗由乎内也。凡伤寒欲解，将汗之时，若其正气内实，邪不能与之争，但汗出自不作战，所谓不战，应知体不虚也。若其人本虚，邪与正争，微者为振，甚则为战，正胜邪则战而汗解矣。故凡邪正之争于外者则为战，战，其愈者也；邪正之争于内者则为栗，栗，其甚者也。论曰：阴中于邪，必内栗也。夫战为正气将复，栗则邪气肆强，故伤寒六七日，有但栗不战，竟成寒逆者，多不可救，此以正气中虚，阴邪内盛，正不胜邪，而反为邪气所胜。凡遇此证，使非用大补温热之剂，及艾灼回阳等法，其他焉得而御之？[52p]

    Sweating and Chills

    Sweating and chills are different; sweating arises from the external, while chills come from the internal. When someone with a cold wants to relieve it, if their vital energy is strong internally, then the evil cannot compete with it. However, when sweating occurs without effort, this is known as non-battle, indicating that the body is not deficient. If a person is inherently weak, and the evil struggles with the righteous, the minor symptoms would cause chills, while severe cases lead to sweating. If the righteous overcomes the evil, then sweating will resolve the condition. Therefore, any struggle between the evil and the righteous occurring externally is called a battle, indicating recovery; while a struggle between evil and righteous internally results in chills, which is more severe. It is said: When the evil dominates within, there must be chills. Sweating signifies the restoration of vital energy, while chills indicate that evil energy is rampant. Thus, if someone suffers from a cold for six to seven days and only experiences chills without sweating, they may develop a reverse cold condition that is very hard to treat. This results from weakness in vital energy and the internal dominance of yin evil, where the righteous do not overcome the evil, leading to the evil prevailing instead. In such cases, it is essential to use powerful warming tonics and rescue yang methods, among others; how else can one counter it?[52p]

    　　　　　头汗

    　　头汗之证有二：一为邪热上壅，一为阳气内脱也。盖头为诸阳之会，凡伤寒遍身得汗者，谓之热越。若身无汗，则热不得越而上蒸阳分，故但头汗出也。治热蒸者，可清可散，甚者可下，在去其热而病自愈。至若气脱一证，则多以妄下伤阴，或克伐太过，或泄泻不止，以致阴竭于下，则阳脱于上，小水不通，而上见头汗，则大危矣。
    　　　　　论治

    　　头汗脉紧数，有表邪当散者，宜小柴胡汤，或柴胡桂枝干姜汤，及新方诸柴胡饮，俱可酌用。若有火邪，脉洪滑，内多烦热，头汗当清者，宜人参白虎汤、益元散之类主之。若水结胸，心下满，头汗出者，或大陷胸汤，或小半夏茯苓汤。若便结腹胀，疼痛头汗者，宜承气汤。若诸虚泄泻，阳脱头汗者，宜独参汤，或大补元煎、六味回阳等饮，作急救之。庶可保全。[53p]

    Head Sweating

    There are two conditions for head sweating: one is due to evil heat obstructing upward, and the other is the internal loss of yang energy. The head is where all yang energies converge. When someone suffers from full-body sweating due to a cold, it is referred to as heat spreading upwards. If there is no sweating from the body, the heat does not disperse and rises to disturb the yang aspect, resulting in only head sweating. The treatment for heat steaming can be either purifying or dispersing; in severe cases, purgation may be needed to eliminate the heat and allow the condition to resolve itself. In the case of energy loss, it is often due to reckless purgation injuring the yin, excessive depletion, or continuous diarrhea, leading to the exhaustion of yin below and the loss of yang above. When there is difficulty in urination and head sweating occurs, it signals great danger.

    Discussion of Treatment

    For head sweating with a tight and rapid pulse, indicating an exterior evil that should be dispersed, Xiao Chai Hu Tang (Minor Bupleurum Decoction) is appropriate, or Chai Hu Gui Zhi Gan Jiang Tang (Bupleurum and Cinnamon Twig Decoction) and various new formulas with Chai Hu can also be used as needed. If there is a fire evil, with a broad and slippery pulse and internal fever, head sweating should be cleared with Ren Shen Bai Hu Tang (Ginseng Powdered White Tiger Decoction) or Yi Yuan San (Benefit Source Powder). If there is water retention in the chest, with fullness under the heart and head sweating, either Da Xian Xiong Tang (Major Sinking Chest Decoction) or Xiao Ban Xia Fu Ling Tang (Minor Pinellia and Poria Decoction) can be used. If there are hard stools, abdominal distension, pain, and head sweating, Cheng Qi Tang (Regulate Qi Decoction) is indicated. For various forms of deficiency, diarrhea, and head sweating with yang loss, Du Shen Tang (Ginseng Decoction) or Da Bu Yuan Jian (Greatly Tonifying Source Decoction) and Liu Wei Hui Yang (Six-Ingredient Restore Yang Decoction) can serve as emergency remedies. This may help preserve life.[53p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　大汗

    　　大汗之病，阳气尽随汗而外越，若不急为止抑，则阳气立散，即时身死。法当以大补之剂煎饮，一线之气可留，而大汗可止。方用人参一两，或黄芪二两代之，当归一两，北五味一钱，桑叶七片，急为煎服。此方即补血汤之变，妙在补气药多于补血，使气旺则血自生，血生则汗可止。况方中加五味子以收汗，如桑叶以止汗，有不相得益彰者乎？倘以大汗之人，气必大喘，不可以参芪重增其气，纯用补血之品，末为无见。然而血不可骤生，气所当急固，不顾气，徒补血，未见功成。此似是而非，又不可不急辨之也。　　凡人无论有病无病，一旦汗如雨出不肯止者，名曰亡阳。汗尽止有气未绝，最危之证也。[54p]

    The Illness of Great Sweating

    When a person suffers from great sweating, the yang energy dissipates alongside the sweat. If not urgently restrained, the yang energy will scatter, resulting in immediate death. The remedy should consist of a potent restorative decoction. If the vital energy is preserved, the excessive sweating can be stopped. One should use one ounce of ginseng, or replace it with two ounces of astragalus; one ounce of angelica, one-tenth of an ounce of North Schisandra berries, and seven pieces of mulberry leaves, and decoct this urgently for consumption. This formula is a variation of the Blood Supplementing Decoction, notable for having more Qi-tonifying herbs than blood-nourishing ones, allowing the Qi to flourish so that the blood can be generated. With the blood generated, sweating can cease. Furthermore, the inclusion of Schisandra berries helps to retain sweat, just as mulberry leaves help to stop sweating; there are complementary benefits here.

    However, in the case of someone experiencing great sweating, the breath must be labored; one cannot simply increase Qi with ginseng and astragalus heavily. Purely relying on blood-replenishing substances will yield limited results. Yet blood cannot be generated abruptly, and the urgent need is for the Qi. Ignoring the Qi and solely focusing on replenishing the blood will not yield success. This distinction must be urgently made.

    In general, whether a person is ill or not, if they suddenly sweat profusely and cannot stop, it is termed loss of yang. Once sweat has ceased but there remains some vital energy, it indicates a critical condition.[54p]

    若因汗出而用止汗之药则汗不能止，若因汗尽而用补血之药则血难骤生，所当急补其气，尚可挽回。然而补气之药，舍人参实无他物可代。方用收汗生阳汤，人参、黄芪、麦冬、熟地各一两，北五味三钱，当归、炒枣仁各五钱，甘草一钱，水煎服。一剂而汗收，再剂而气复，三剂而气旺，四剂而身健矣。此方之妙，妙在气血均补，而尤补于气，使气足以生阳，阳旺而阴亦生矣。夫亡阳之证，虽是阳亡，其实阴虚不能摄阳，以致阳气之亡也。倘阴足以摄阳，则汗虽出，何至亡阳？然治亡阳之证，乌可徒救阳乎？救阳兼救阴也。　　大汗势必用补气之药，以救亡阳之证，然而过用补气之药，仍恐阳旺而阴消，服数剂补气药后，即宜改用补阴之品。况亡阳之后，阴血正枯，进以补水之药，正投其所好也。阴定则阳生，阴阳无偏胜之弊矣。[55p]

    If sweating arises and one uses medicine to stop the sweat, then the sweating cannot be stopped. If sweating is excessive and one uses blood-tonifying medicine, then blood will not quickly regenerate. The urgent matter is to replenish the qi, which can still be restored. However, among qi-tonifying medicines, ginseng truly cannot be substituted for anything else. One should use the Sweat-Collecting and Yang-Replenishing Decoction, which includes one tael each of ginseng, astragalus, ophiopogon, and cooked rehmannia, three qian of north five-flavor fruit, five qian each of angelica and roasted jujube seed, and one qian of licorice, boiled in water to take. After one dose, the sweating will cease; after two doses, the qi will be restored; after three doses, the qi will be vigorous; after four doses, the body will be healthy. The essence of this formula lies in the balanced replenishment of qi and blood, especially focusing on qi, which provides enough energy to generate yang. When yang is abundant, yin will also be produced. In cases of yang deficiency, although yang is lost, in fact, it is due to yin deficiency that cannot contain yang, resulting in the loss of yang qi. If yin were sufficient to contain yang, then even if sweating occurs, there would be no loss of yang. However, in treating yang deficiency, how can one only seek to restore yang? One must restore both yang and yin.

    Profuse sweating necessitates the use of qi-tonifying medicine to rescue the condition of yang deficiency. However, if qi-tonifying medicine is overused, there is still a fear that yang will become exuberant while yin dissipates. After taking several doses of qi-tonifying medicine, it is advisable to shift to tonifying yin products. Moreover, after the loss of yang, yin and blood are indeed depleted, so providing water-tonifying medicine corresponds perfectly to this situation. When yin is stabilized, yang will flourish, eliminating the issue of one side being overly dominant.[55p]

    　　　　　头手汗

    　　凡人头顶出汗，乃肾火有余而肾水不足。若不知其故，而徒用止汗之药，必致目昏而耳痛，法当滋其肾而清肺金之化源，自易奏功如向。方用桑叶一斤，熟地二斤，北五味三两，麦冬六两，各为末，蜜为丸，每日白滚水送下五钱或一两，一月后永不出汗矣。更有人每饭之时，头汗如雨落者，此又胃火胜而非肾火余也，法当用元参、麦冬、天冬、生地各一斤，北五味四两，酸枣仁半斤，各为末，蜜为丸，每日白滚水送下一两，二月必愈。[56p]

    Head Sweating

    When a person's head sweats, it is due to an excess of kidney fire and a deficiency of kidney water. If one does not understand the reason and merely uses sweat-stopping medicines, it will surely lead to dizziness and ear pain. The method should be to nourish the kidneys and clear the source of lung transformation, which will naturally be effective. The prescription includes one pound of mulberry leaves, two pounds of cooked rehmannia, three taels of north five-flavor herb, and six taels of ophiopogon, all ground into powder, then formed into pills with honey. Take five qian or one liang daily with hot water, and after a month, sweating will cease forever.

    Additionally, if there is excessive head sweating during meals, it is due to excess stomach fire rather than residual kidney fire. The method here should incorporate one pound each of scrophularia, ophiopogon, tian dong, and raw rehmannia, four taels of north five-flavor herb, and half a pound of sour jujube seed, all ground into powder and formed into pills with honey. Take one liang daily with hot water, and one will certainly recover within two months.[56p]

    似乎胃火胜，宜用竹叶石膏汤，而余偏不用者何也？盖胃火之胜者微胜耳，非若炽盛而火炎，奔腾而热发，不过因饮食之味，入于胃中，遂觉津津汗出，饮食完而汗随止，然则以元参一味解之有余矣。况又用天麦二冬以清肺火，生地以凉血，酸枣仁以平心火，五味子以收汗而滋液，则胃经有火之盛，亦已消磨，况原未十分之盛乎？此敛法之一也。手中之汗，细小病也，不必入于此中，以药水洗之愈。　　洗手汗出，方用黄芪、葛根各一两，荆芥、防风各三钱，水煎汤一盆，热熏而温洗三次即无汗，神方也。即是此汤亦可然不若每日一换药之为妙也。[57p]

    It seems that stomach fire is somewhat dominant, and bamboo leaf gypsum decoction is recommended, but why do I prefer not to use it? It is because the stomach fire is only slightly elevated, not intensely raging and fiery, merely because of the flavors from food entering the stomach, leading to slight perspiration. Once the meal is finished, the sweating also ceases. Therefore, resolving it with just a single ingredient like Scrophularia is sufficient. Furthermore, using ingredients like Tianma, two types of Dong, to clear lung fire, and Shengdi to cool the blood, as well as Suanzaoren to calm heart fire and Wuweizi to control sweating and nourish fluids, will also diminish the stomach's fiery state, especially since it was not excessively strong to begin with. This is one method of moderation. The sweat from the hands is a minor issue, and there's no need to involve this treatment; washing them with water would suffice.

    For the hand sweating, one would use one ounce each of Astragalus and Kudzu, and three qian each of Schizonepeta and Ledebouriella, boiling them in water to prepare a basin of decoction, then steaming and washing the hands three times while warm, which will eliminate the sweat—a marvelous remedy. This decoction can be used this way, but it is even better to change the herbs daily.[57p]

    The following is the translation of the provided Classical Chinese text:

    Right, divide into three doses, simmer with ginger water.

    Huangqi Liu Yi Decoction treats deficiencies in men and women, spontaneous sweating, night sweats, fatigue in the limbs, restlessness in the chest, frequent thirst, dryness in the lips and mouth, a wan and sallow complexion, inability to eat or drink, and is often taken to nourish qi and blood, calm and harmonize the organs. Huangqi six taels, remove the reed and honey-roast; licorice one tael, roasted. Each dose is five qian, with one cup of water and one jujube, simmer until reduced to seven parts, and take warm at any time. One formula adds Bai Zhu and Bai Shao.

    Yupingfeng Powder [from "De Xiaofang"]
    Fangfeng and Huangqi each one tael, Bai Zhu two taels. Each dose is three qian, with two cups of water and three slices of ginger, simmer until reduced to six parts, and take warm at any time.

    Tiaowei Decoction [from Dong Yuan] treats excess damp leading to spontaneous sweating, supplements weak Wei qi, and addresses exterior deficiency that cannot withstand cold. Huangqi and Ma Huang root each one qian, fresh licorice leaf, Angelica leaf, fresh Huangqin, Banxia washed seven times, each five fen; Polyporus and Qianghuo each seven fen; Maidengdong with the heart removed, fresh Dihuang each three fen; Schisandra seeds seven seeds; Suomu and Honghua each one fen. Grind as large as a soybean, make one dose, with two cups of water, simmer to one cup, strain and take warm. In cases of stroke, spontaneous sweating must be treated with caution as excessive sweating shouldn't be induced again, hence the use of Ma Huang is restricted to its root. One edition omits Banxia.[62p]

    　　右作一服，水二锺，姜五片，枣二枚，煎至一锺，食前服。本方加黄芪二钱，名黄芪建中汤，治虚劳自汗。加当归，名当归建中汤，治妇人血虚自汗。其自汗漏不止者，加桂一钱，熟附子半个，名桂枝附子汤，煎空心服。[63p]

    Qiang Huo Sheng Shi Decoction treats damp phlegm and spontaneous sweating. It consists of:

    • 30 grams of roasted licorice,
    • 30 grams of ginseng,
    • 22.5 grams of astragalus,
    • 15 grams of raw baical skullcap,
    • 15 grams of wine-soaked baical skullcap,
    • 15 grams of chuanxiong,
    • 10 grams of asarum,
    • 10 grams of sophora root,
    • 10 grams of vitex,
    • 10 grams of fangfeng,
    • 6 grams of angelica,
    • 2.5 grams of meridian herb,
    • 2.5 grams of bupleurum,
    • 1 gram of mint.

    Prepare one dose with two cups of water, simmer down to one and a half cups, then add asarum and the other four ingredients, simmer further until one cup remains, and take warm.

    Li Qi Jiang Tan Decoction treats damp phlegm and spontaneous sweating. It contains:

    • 12 grams of platycodon,
    • 12 grams of stir-fried bitter orange peel,
    • 12 grams of tangerine peel,
    • 12 grams of stir-fried pinellia,
    • 12 grams of poria,
    • 12 grams of cyperus soaked in child’s urine,
    • 12 grams of fritillaria,
    • 5 grams of raw licorice,
    • 5 grams of cinnamon twig.

    Use two cups of water, simmer down to eight parts, and take it away from meals.

    Jian Zhong Decoction treats spontaneous sweating due to exterior deficiency. It consists of:

    • 25 grams of peony,
    • 6 grams of cinnamon,
    • 6 grams of roasted licorice.

    Prepare one dose with two cups of water, add five slices of ginger and two jujubes, and simmer until one cup remains. Take it before meals. This formula can be modified by adding 6 grams of astragalus, called Huang Qi Jian Zhong Decoction for treating deficiency-related spontaneous sweating. Adding 6 grams of angelica gives rise to Dang Gui Jian Zhong Decoction for treating women's blood deficiency with spontaneous sweating. If spontaneous sweating is incessant, add 10 grams of cinnamon and half a piece of prepared aconite, known as Gui Zhi Fu Zi Decoction, and take it on an empty stomach.[63p]

    　　白朮散河间　治虚风多汗，食则汗出如洗，少气痿劣，久不治，必为消渴证。　　牡蛎煅，三钱　白朮一两二钱半　防风二两半　　右为末，每服一钱，温水调下，不拘时候。如恶风，倍防风、白朮。如多汗面肿，倍牡蛎。

    Bai Zhu San (White Atractylodes Powder) for Treating Wind-Phantom Excessive Sweating:
    This formula is effective for wind-induced excessive sweating, where sweating occurs profusely like washing, with weak vitality; if not treated for a long time, it will surely lead to symptoms of diabetes.

    Ingredients:

    • Calcined Oyster Shell: 9 grams
    • Bai Zhu (White Atractylodes): 37.5 grams
    • Fang Feng (Siler Root): 150 grams

    Prepare as a powder. Take 3 grams each time mixed with warm water, without regard to timing. If there is wind discomfort, double the amounts of Fang Feng and Bai Zhu. If there is excessive sweating with facial swelling, double the amount of Oyster Shell.

    An Wei Decoction (Comforting the Stomach) [by Dong Yuan]:
    This formula treats sweating induced by eating and drinking, leading to prolonged heart vacuity, where wind-void evil intrudes, causing hemiplegia and symptoms of stroke. First, relieve the sweating and then suppress the rebellious Qi.

    Ingredients:

    • Huang Lian (Coptis): Remove the beard
    • Wu Wei Zi (Schisandra): 5 grams
    • Wu Mei (Mume Fruit): 5 grams of pulp
    • Sheng Gan Cao (Raw Licorice): 5 grams
    • Shu Gan Cao (Cooked Licorice): 3 grams
    • Sheng Ma (Black Cohosh): 2 grams

    Use 2 cups of water, decoct to 1 cup, and take warm far from meals. Avoid damp ingredients, wine, and strong spices.

    Mu Li San (Oyster Shell Powder) [from San Yin]:
    Used for general Qi deficiency and sudden onset weakness, where fluids are not stable and sweating occurs frequently. It also treats persistent night sweats.

    Ingredients:

    • Huang Qi (Astragalus)
    • Ma Huang Gen (Ephedra Root)
    • Calcined Oyster Shell: equal parts

    Grind the above into a powder. Take 9 grams with 1.5 cups of water and a pinch of wheat, decoct until reduced to 2/3. Take warm at any time. The formula "De Xiao Fang" also contains Zhi Mu (Anemarrhena) and has each of the three ingredients at 37.5 grams, alongside Bai Zhu at 18.75 grams and Gan Cao at 7.5 grams.[64p]

    　　大补黄芪汤魏氏　治阴阳偏虚，自汗盗汗。　　黄芪蜜炙　防风　山茱萸肉　当归　白朮炒　肉桂　川芎　炙甘草　五味子　人参各一两　白茯苓一两半　熟地二两　肉苁蓉酒浸，三两　　每服五钱，水二锺，姜三片，枣二枚，煎八分，不拘时温服。

    Da Bu Huang Qi Tang by the Wei Family
    Treats deficiency of yin and yang, spontaneous sweating and night sweating.
    Ingredients: Honey-fried Astragalus, Fang Feng, He Shou Wu flesh, Dong Quai, roasted Bai Zhu, Cinnamon, Chuan Xiong, honey-fried Gan Cao, Schisandra fruit, Ginseng each 1 tael; Bai Fu Ling 1.5 taels; cooked Di Huang 2 taels; meat of Herba Cistanches soaked in wine, 3 taels.
    Dosage: Take 5 qian with 2 sheng of water, 3 slices of ginger, 2 dates, decoct to 8 parts, warm to drink at any time.

    Shi Biao San (from "Dan Liao")
    Treats colds, with loose pores, spontaneous sweating.
    Ingredients: Prepared Fu Zi, meat of Herba Cistanches, roasted Xi Xin, Schisandra fruit each 1 tael.
    Preparation: Grind the above and mix with Huang Qi Jian Zhong Tang to harmonize; add ginger and dates according to the original formula, with stir-fried floating wheat for decocting. Take for 3-4 doses as needed.

    Huang Qi Tang (from "Ji Sheng")
    Treats joy, anger, shock, fear, and deficiency in the bedroom, leading to deficiency of yin and yang, either causing sudden sweat or unceasing night sweat.
    Ingredients: Honey-fried Astragalus, 1.5 taels; Bai Fu Ling; cooked Di Huang steamed in yellow wine; unburnt Cinnamon; Tian Men Dong; Ma Huang Gen; Long Gu each 1 tael; Schisandra fruit; roasted wheat; Fang Feng; Dong Quai soaked in wine then lightly fried; honey-fried Gan Cao each 0.5 tael.
    Preparation: Grind and sift the above. Take 4 qian, brewed with 5 slices of fresh ginger at any time. For sudden sweat from shock, add cooked Fu Zi. For fever with spontaneous sweating, add Shi Hu. If ineffective, consider eating more flour products for relief.[65p]

    Warming Powder - Stops sweating.
    Chuanxiong, Baizhi, and dried roots, each one tael; rice powder three taels. Grind together into a fine powder, and use cotton to wrap it and pat it onto the body.

    Red Powder - Stops sweating.
    Mahuang root and calcined oyster, each one tael; red stone resin and dragon bone, each half tael. Grind together into a fine powder, store it in a silk bag, and use it like powder.

    Sweat-Stopping Powder
    Mahuang root, oyster powder, burnt fan ash, and (trailing vine) root, each three taels; Atractylodes two taels; rice powder three sheng. Grind into a fine powder, mix well, store in a silk bag, and apply to the body two to three times a day. Avoid peaches, plums, and sparrow meat. Also, moxibustion of the Dazhui point with five to six hundred cones, performed two to seven times a day, can help stop sweat gradually.

    Yin-Collecting Powder - Treats all types of spontaneous sweating, night sweat, and issues caused by wind, where sweating is excessive and cannot be stopped by other medications.
    Mahuang root, dried roots, Baizhi, calcined oyster, and dragon bone, each half tael; rice powder two taels; half a qian of brain matter. Grind into a fine powder and wrap it in gauze to apply to the areas of sweating until it stops.

    Astragalus Decoction - Treats spontaneous sweating.
    Coton Astragalus and aged tangerine peel, each one and a half tael.[66p]

    The right is a fine powder; each dose is three qian. Use one he of hemp seeds, grind them thoroughly, and mix with water to extract one cup of liquid. Strain out the residue in a silver or stone vessel and simmer until cream rises. Then add a large spoonful of honey and continue to boil until bubbling, and mix in the medicinal powder. Take on an empty stomach. This also treats elderly people with severe constipation; two doses can cure the condition.

    Danggui Liu Huang Decoction treats yin deficiency and night sweats.
    Ingredients: 1 qian of danggui, sheng dihuang, shu dihuang, huangbai, huangqin, huanglian; each 1 qian, and 2 qian of huangqi. Prepare one dose with two cups of water, simmer until one cup remains, and take before lying down.

    Zhengqi Decoction treats damp-heat disorders, characterized by slight sweating, mild yellowing of the urine, and easy urination.
    Ingredients: 1 qian of fried huangbai, 1.5 qian of fried zhi mu, and 0.5 qian of roasted licorice. Grind these into a coarse powder, prepare one dose with two cups of water, simmer down to one cup, and take at bedtime. In Hejian, where zhi mu is not available, they use zhi zi (gardenia) and call it zhi zi huang pi decoction, which treats similar symptoms.

    Fangfeng Powder treats night sweats.
    Ingredients: 5 qian of fangfeng, 2.5 qian of chuanxiong, and 1.25 qian of ginseng. Grind these into a fine powder; each dose is 2 qian, to be mixed with rice drink before bed.

    Baizhu Powder treats night sweats.
    Use any amount of baizhu, shredded into small pieces, and 1 sheng of floating wheat. Boil with water until dry; if the baizhu is still hard, add an additional 1 or 2 sheng of water, boil until soft, then remove the wheat. Cut into slices, dry them, and grind into a fine powder. Each dose is 2 to 3 qian, taken at any time, and can be mixed with simmered floating wheat soup.[67p]

    　　麦煎散　治荣卫不调，夜多盗汗，四肢烦疼，饮食进退，面黄肌瘦，并皆治之。　　柴胡　鳖甲酢煮三五十沸，去裙襕，再用酢炙黄　秦艽各二两　干漆炒烟尽　人参　白茯苓　干葛　川乌炮去皮尖　元参各一两　　右为细末，每服二钱，先用小麦三七粒，煎汤一盏，去麦入药，再煎三五沸，食后服。

    Mai Jian San treats disharmony of the protective and nutritive qi, excessive night sweating, pain in the limbs, fluctuations in appetite, a pale face and thin skin, all of which can be addressed by this formula.

    Chai Hu, Bie Jia (turtle shell), boiled in vinegar for 30-50 minutes, remove the skirt and further roast with vinegar until browned. Qin Jiao, each two liang, Gan Qi (dry lacquer), stir-fried until the smoke dissipates, Ren Shen (ginseng), Bai Fu Ling, Gan Geng (dry kudzu), Chuan Wu (large-leaf monkshood) prepared by removing skin and tips, and Yuan Shen, each one liang.

    Grind all ingredients into a fine powder. Each dosage is two qian, first use 37 small wheat grains, boil in one cup of water, remove the wheat and add the powdered medicine, boil for another 3-5 minutes, and take after meals.

    Da Jian Zhong Tang treats symptoms of deficiency heat, night sweats, body aches in the joints, lower back pain, fatigue in the body and limbs, gradual weakness, bitter mouth and dry tongue, heart palpitations, and shortness of breath. Mian Huang Qi (honey-roasted astragalus), Yuan Zhi (polygala) cooked without its heart, Dang Gui (Chinese angelica) washed with wine, and Ze Xie (water plantain) each two qian, Bai Shao (white peony), Long Gu (dragon bone) calcined, Ren Shen (ginseng) each one and a half qian, and Zhi Gan Cao (honey-roasted licorice) one qian.

    Prepare one dose with two zhongs (measures) of water and five slices of ginger, boil to yield one zhong, and take before meals. If energy is weak, add two qian of Pa Gradiculus (Aconitum carmichaelii). For back pain and stiff tendons, add one qian of peeled Guang Gui (cinnamon).

    Another formula for treating night sweats, where bedding and clothing are soaked: Ma Huang Gen (ephedra root), Mu Li (oyster shell) calcined, each three liang, Huang Qi (astragalus), and Ren Shen (ginseng) each two liang, Long Gu (dragon bone) crushed, and Gou Qi Gen (goji root) and Bai Pi (white skin of trees) each four liang, with seven dates split open.

    Chop the ingredients, add six sheng (liters) of water, boil down to two and a half sheng, strain out the residue, divide into six warm doses. If walking eight or nine miles, repeat the dosage, and finish within one day. Avoid hot foods like garlic and flour products.[68p]

    Bai Zi Ren Pill (from "Ben Shi Fang"): It restrains yang energy, stops night sweats, promotes eating and drinking, and dispels heat from the meridians.

    Calcified oyster shell is treated to remove inner fire, roasted with wine seven times and dried. Ingredients include:

    • Ginseng
    • Ephedra root, slowly roasted and wiped to remove sweat
    • Atractylodes
    • Schisandra, each one liang
    • Clean wheat bran roasted for half a liang
    • Bai Zi Ren
    • Ban Xia Qu, each two liang

    Grind them into powder, form into pills the size of a paulownia seed. Take three to five dozen pills with a hollow grain drink, two times a day. If effective, reduce by one dose; if cured, stop. It can also be made into powder.[69p]

    Jiao Mu San - For treatment of night sweats that persist for a long time.
    Jiao Mu (pepper eye) and Ma Huang (ephedra) in equal parts.
    Grind them into a fine powder; take one qian each time, mixed with warm, non-hot wine after meals.

    Another Formula - For treating night sweats due to external kidney dampness.
    Ren Shen (ginseng), Ku Shen (bitter root), Long Dan Cao (gentian), and Ma Huang (ephedra), each three qian.
    Grind these into a powder, process with honey into pills the size of a wu tong seed. Take thirty pills each time, taken with boiled wheat broth.

    Da Bu Yuan Jian - For treating severe damage to qi and blood in men and women, loss of spirit, and symptoms like self-sweating and night sweats.
    Ren Shen: one or two qian; if more, then one or two liang.
    Shan Yao (Chinese yam) and Du Zhong (eucommia) each two qian.
    Bei Gui (angelica root) should be removed if it causes diarrhea.
    Gou Qi Zi (wolfberry) two to three qian.
    Shu Di Huang (cooked rehmannia): two to three qian if less; two to three liang if more.
    Zhi Gan Cao (honey-fried licorice): one or two qian.
    Shan Zhu Yu (cornelian cherry) one qian; remove if sensitive to sour or unable to swallow sour.
    Use two sheng (about two pints) of water, boil down to seven parts, take warm before meals.

    Yi Yin Jian - For cases of true yin deficiency in kidney water, presenting symptoms of predominantly yang pulse and signs, with signs of internal heat and self-sweating due to yin deficiency.
    Dan Mai (red peony), Mai Dong (ophiopogon), Shao Yao (peony), Sheng Di (raw rehmannia), each two qian;
    Gan Cao (licorice) one qian;
    Shu Di (cooked rehmannia) three to five qian;
    Niu Xi (achyranthes) one and a half qian.
    Use two sheng of water, boil down to seven parts, take warm before meals.[70p]

    Jiajian Yiyin Decoction: For conditions as previously described, this is suitable when heat is pronounced. Ingredients: 2 qian each of raw Rehmannia, peony, and Ophiopogon; 3 to 5 qian of cooked Rehmannia; 5 to 7 fen of honey-fried licorice; 1 qian each of Anemarrhena and Dioscorea; 2 zhong of water, decoct and take.

    Sanyin Decoction: For those with insufficient essence and blood without heat. Ingredients: 2 to 3 qian of Angelica, 3 to 5 qian of cooked Rehmannia, 1 qian of honey-fried licorice, 2 qian each of wine-fried peony and jujube seed, ginseng as needed; 2 zhong of water, decoct to 7 parts, take away from meals.

    Wuyin Decoction: For true yin deficiency and symptoms such as spontaneous sweating due to spleen deficiency. Ingredients: 5 to 7 qian or 1 liang of cooked Rehmannia; 2 qian each of fried peony and fried yam; 2 to 3 qian of fried adzuki bean; 1.5 qian of Poria; 20 grains of Schisandra; ginseng as needed; 1 to 2 qian each of fried Atractylodes and honey-fried licorice; 2 zhong of water, add 20 grains of lotus seed without heart, decoct and take.

    Liuwèi Huayang Drink: For spontaneous sweating and symptoms of impending yin and yang collapse. Ingredients: 1 liang or several qian of ginseng; 2 to 3 qian of processed Aconite and roasted dry ginger; 1 qian of honey-fried licorice; 5 qian or 1 liang of cooked Rehmannia; 3 qian of Angelica; 2 zhong of water, boil with strong fire to 7 or 8 parts, take warm.[71p]

    Five Gentlemen Decoction: Used for treating deficiency-cold of the spleen and stomach, with symptoms of spontaneous sweating, diarrhea, and dampness.     Preserve Yin Decoction: Treats all forms of Yin deficiency with internal heat, excessive sweating, and blood movement disorders. Ingredients: 2 qian each of raw and cooked rehmannia and peony, 1.5 qian each of Chinese yam, Sichuan Dipsacus, huangqin (scutellaria), and huangbo (berberis), and 1 qian of raw licorice. Use 2 sheng of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm after meals.

    Clearing Transformation Decoction: Treats women who experience heat after childbirth and symptoms of blood heat causing erratic behavior, Yin deficiency with excessive sweating, and unresolved fire symptoms. Ingredients: 2 qian each of peony and ophiopogon, 2-3 qian each of moutan, poria, huangqin, and raw rehmannia, and 1 qian of dendrobium. Use 2.5 sheng of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm after meals.

    Single Formula

    For night sweats: Mix powdered five-leaf gall and buckwheat flour in equal parts. Combine with water to make cakes and steam until cooked. In the night, eat 2-3 when hungry, avoiding tea or water; it is very effective.

    For spontaneous and night sweats: For spontaneous sweating, apply five-leaf gall powder mixed with saliva into the navel and bind it; it will stop in one night.[72p]

    　　　　针炙

    　　《灵枢》曰：无刺漉漉之汗。漉漉之汗，邪盛在肌腠也。　　骨寒热者，病无所安，汗注不休，齿末槁，取其少阴于阴股之络。齿已槁，死不治。骨厥亦然。　　病始手臂者，先取手阳明太阴而汗出。病始头首者，先取项太阳而汗出。病始足胫者，先取足阳明而汗出。臂太阴可汗出，足阳明可汗出。故取阴而汗出，甚者止之于阳；取阳而汗出，甚者止之于阴。　　热病已得汗出而脉尚躁，喘且复热，勿刺肤。喘甚者死。　　热病而汗且出，及脉顺可汗者，取之鱼际、太渊、大都、太白。泻之则热去，补之则汗出。汗出太甚，取内踝上横脉以止之。　　五禁五套五逆者，皆不可刺。曰大汗出之后，是三夺也。　　《医学纲目》曰：盗汗，取阴都、五里、间使。　　盗汗，取中极、气海。[77p]

    Foot Sweat: Regardless of how abundant the yang fluff is, if one boils water to wash the feet and spreads it inside the shoe, it can alleviate the issue.
    Persistent Foot Sweat: Burn earth within the living quarters, spread it inside the shoe, and it will help.

    Acupuncture
    The "Lingshu" states: one should not pierce when there is excessive sweat. Excessive sweat indicates that evil has settled in the skin and flesh. For those suffering from bone chill and heat, the disease has nowhere to settle, and the sweat pours out continuously, leading to dry teeth. One should target the Shaoyin channels in the inner thigh. Once the teeth are dry, it's beyond cure. The same applies to bone qi stagnation.
    For diseases starting in the arms, one should first target the Yangming and Taiyin points to induce sweating. For diseases starting in the head, one targets the Taiyang. For diseases starting in the legs, one targets the Yangming of the feet. The Taiyin of the arms can induce sweating, as can the Yangming of the feet. Thus, one should target the yin to induce sweat, and for severe cases, stop at the yang; target the yang to induce sweat, and for severe cases, stop at the yin.
    In cases of febrile illness where sweating has occurred but the pulse remains restless, and there is panting along with continued heat, do not pierce the skin. Severe panting leads to death.
    In a febrile illness with sweating and a steady pulse, one can induce sweat by targeting the fish border, Taiyuan, Dadu, and Taibai points. By draining, the heat is released; by supplementing, the sweat is encouraged to flow. If sweating is excessive, stop it by targeting the lateral ankle's transverse pulse.
    Those with five prohibitions, five bindings, and five reversals must not be pierced. It states that excessive sweating thereafter leads to three losses.
    The "Medical Essentials" states: For night sweats, target Yindu, Wuli, and Jianshi points.
    For night sweats, target the Zhongji and Qihai points. [77p]

    　　虚损盗汗劳热，取百劳三分，泻三吸；肺俞四分，补三呼。
    　　　　导引

    　　《保生秘要》曰：自汗盗汗导引法，先念脐想火于内旋转，又以手覆脐念，次想脐下一条水，下膀胱，上尾闾，又至背，穿出心头洗之。非遗精不用行脐下一条水法。　　无故自汗是热炽盛，使升水降火法，其汗即退。
    　　　　医案

    　　《东垣十书》曰：张芸夫己酉四月，天寒阴雨，寒湿相杂，因官事饮食失节，劳役所伤，病解之后，汗出不止，沾濡数日，恶寒重添厚衣，心胸闷躁，时躁热，头目昏愦，壅塞，食少减，此乃胃外阴火炽盛，与夫雨之湿气挟热，两气相合，令湿热大作，汗出不休，兼见风邪以助东方甲乙，以风药去其燥，以甘药泻其热，羌活胜湿汤主之，一服而止，诸证悉去。[78p]

    Sweating due to deficiency and night sweats caused by heat should have three portions of diuretics taken and then three portions of tonics after purging. For the lungs, four portions should be tonified while three breaths are aided.

    Guidance

    The "Essentials of Life Preservation" states that for spontaneous and nocturnal sweating, one should first focus on the navel, envisioning fire circulating within, then cover the navel with the hands while imagining a stream of water descending from the navel, moving down to the bladder and tips of the tailbone, and then to the back, emerging from the heart to cleanse it. There is no need to use the method of guiding water under the navel if there is no loss of essence. Spontaneous sweating without cause is a result of excessive heat; hence, one must lower the fire and elevate the water to stop the sweating.

    Medical Case

    According to the "Ten Books of Dongyuan": In April of the Ren Yin year, Zhang Yun experienced cold and rainy weather mixed with dampness. Poor diet and excessive labor due to official matters resulted in an illness that led to prolonged sweating. After recovery, he continued to sweat without stopping for several days and felt severe chills, demanding thicker clothing. He experienced tightness in the chest, restlessness, intermittent fever, dizziness, and food reduction. This was due to excessive external Yin fire from the stomach, compounded by moist heat from the rain, which intensified the accumulation of moist heat, resulting in persistent sweating. Furthermore, a wind pathogen coupled with the elements of the eastern auspicious direction contributed to his condition. Wind herbs were used to alleviate dryness, and sweet herbs were used to purge heat. The Qianghuo Shengshi Decoction was the main prescription, and just one dose alleviated all symptoms.[78p]

    　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：真定府武德卿年四十六岁，至元丙子三月间，因忧思劳役，饮食失节得病，肢体冷，口鼻气亦凉，额上冷汗出，时发昏愦，六脉如蛛丝。一医作风证，欲以宣风散下之。予因思钱氏《小儿论》制宣风散，谓小儿内伤脾胃，或吐或泻，久则风邪陷入胃中而作飧泄，散中有结，恐传慢惊，以宣风散导去风邪。《内经》云：久风为飧泄，正此谓也。今德卿形证，乃阴盛阳虚，苦寒之剂，非所宜也。《内经》云：阴气有余，为多汗身寒。又阴阳应象论云：阴盛则身寒汗出，身常清，数栗而寒，寒则厥。调经篇亦云：阴盛生内寒。岐伯曰：厥气上逆，寒气积于胸中而不泻，不泻则温气去寒独留，故寒中。东垣解云：此脾胃不足，劳役形体，中焦营气受病，末传寒中，惟宜补阳。遂以理中汤加黑附子，每服五钱，多用葱白煎羊肉汤，取清汁一大盏调服之。至夕，四肢渐温，汗出少。夜深再服，翌日精神出，六脉生，数服而愈。[79p]

    The "Hygiene Treasure" states: In the 46th year of age, Duke Wu of Zhen Ding, during the third month of the Bingzi year of the Yuan dynasty, fell ill due to worry and overwork, resulting in irregular eating habits. His limbs were cold, and his breath was cool in his mouth and nose. Cold sweat broke out on his forehead, and he often felt dizzy, with his six pulses thin like a spider's thread. One physician diagnosed a wind condition and attempted to treat it with a wind-dispersing powder. I recalled that in Qian's "Treatise on Children," it was mentioned that a child's internal injury to the spleen and stomach could lead to either vomiting or diarrhea, and if prolonged, wind evil could invade the stomach, causing diarrhea and a bound condition. This might lead to lingering surprise, thus the wind-dispersing powder would expel the wind evil. The "Inner Canon" states that prolonged wind can cause diarrhea—that is exactly the case. Now, with Duke Wu's physical symptoms, it is a condition of excessive Yin and deficient Yang, and bitter-cold medicines are not appropriate. The "Inner Canon" says that excessive Yin leads to profuse sweating and coldness. Moreover, the treatise on the correspondence between Yin and Yang states that when Yin is excessive, the body becomes cold, sweating occurs, the body feels persistently cool, and one experiences chills. Coldness causes dysfunction. The "Regulation of the Menstrual Cycle" also states that excessive Yin generates internal cold. Qi Bo said that reverse Qi rises and cold accumulates in the chest without relieving itself; if it does not relieve, warm Qi leaves, and cold remains, thus causing internal cold. Dongyuan explains that this indicates insufficient spleen and stomach energy due to overwork, leading to illness in the middle burner, transmitting cold inward, and thus only yang should be supplemented. Therefore, I prescribed the "Li Zhong Decoction" with added black aconite, taking five qian for each dose, and recommended the broth of lamb cooked with scallions, taking one large cup of the clear juice to mix and consume. By evening, his limbs gradually warmed, and he perspired slightly. Late at night, he took a second dose, and by the next day, his spirit was restored, with six pulses strong; after several doses, he was cured.[79p]

    　　刑部侍郎王立甫之婿，年二十五岁，至元丁卯十一月间，因劳役忧思烦恼，饮食失节而病，身发躁热，肢体困倦，盗汗湿透其衾，不思饮食，气不足一息，面色青黄不泽，请予治之，具说前证。诊其脉浮数而短濇，两寸极小。予告曰：此危证也，治虽粗安，至春必死，当令亲家知之。夫人不以为然，遂易医。至正月燥热而卒。异日立甫同外郎张介夫来谓予曰：吾婿果如君言，愿闻其理。予曰：此非难知也。[80p]

    The son-in-law of the Vice Minister of Justice, Wang Lifu, was twenty-five years old. In the eleventh month of the 丁卯 year of the Yuan dynasty, due to labor and worries, he became ill from stress, losing his appetite and adversely affecting his health. He experienced restlessness, a feverish body, fatigue in his limbs, and profuse sweating that soaked his blankets. He had no desire to eat, his breath was weak, and his complexion was pale and yellow. I was asked to treat him and he provided details of his previous conditions. Upon examining his pulse, it was floating, rapid, and short, with two inches very small. I warned that this was a dangerous condition; although treatment might be simple, he would surely die by spring, and I advised his in-laws to be aware of this. The lady did not believe it and subsequently changed doctors. By the first month, he succumbed to his illness due to heat and distress. On another day, Lifu came with an official named Zhang Jiefu and said to me: "Our son-in-law turned out to be as you said; I wish to understand the rationale." I replied: "This is not difficult to comprehend."[80p]

    《内经》曰：主胜逆，客胜从，天之道也。盖时令为客，人身为主，冬三月人皆惧寒，独渠躁热盗汗，是令不固其阳，时不胜其热，天地时令尚不能制，药何能为？冬乃闭藏之月，阳气当伏于九泉之下，至春发为雷，动为风，鼓坼万物，此奉生之道也。如冬藏不固，则春生不茂，又有疫疠之灾。且人身阳气，亦当伏潜于内，不敢妄扰，无泄皮肤，使气亟夺，此冬藏之应也。令婿汗出于闭藏之月，肾水已涸，至春何以生木？阳气内绝，无所滋荣，不死何待！二君乃叹息而去。[81p]

    The "Inner Canon" says: The master prevails over the inverse, while the guest prevails in acquiescence; this is the way of Heaven. Indeed, the seasons are the guest, while the human body is the master. During the three months of winter, everyone fears the cold, yet there are those who are restless and hot, sweating excessively. This causes their Yang to not be firmly retained, and the season cannot overcome their heat. If even the time and seasons cannot be controlled, how can medicine help? Winter is the month of closure and storage. The Yang energy should lie dormant beneath the nine springs until spring arrives with thunder, stirring everything into movement, which is the way of nurturing life. If the winter storage is not secure, then the spring growth will be weak, leading to epidemics and calamities. Moreover, the Yang energy of the human body should also lie dormant within, not to be recklessly disturbed, nor should the skin be allowed to leak, causing Qi to be rapidly depleted; this is the response to winter storage. Allowing sweat to flow during the month of closure and storage means the kidney water has already dried up; how can life flourish in spring? If the Yang energy within is severed, there is nothing to nourish and flourish—how can one survive? The two gentlemen then sighed and departed.[81p]

    　　《医学正传》曰：上湖吕俊文得内伤虚证，发热自汗，如雨不止，服补中益气汤十数贴不效，予以前方加减，每贴用蜜制黄芪一钱半，人参一钱，白朮、陈皮、甘草各七分，当归、白芍药各一钱，升麻、柴胡各一分，加桂枝三分、麻黄根七分、浮小麦一撮、炮附子三分，三贴而汗止，热亦退而安。
    　　《医学纲目》曰：一男子手足汗，医用芩、连、蘗并补剂皆不效；又足汗常多，后以八物、半、苓为君，白附、川乌佐之，其汗即无。[82p]

    The "Treatise on Medicine" states: At Shanghu, Lu Junwen developed symptoms of internal injury with deficiency, experiencing fever and spontaneous sweating that continuously poured down like rain. After taking the Tonifying Middle and Benefiting Qi Decoction for over ten doses without effect, I modified the prescription. Each dose included one and a half qian of honey-prepared astragalus, one qian of ginseng, seven fen each of white atractylodes, dried tangerine peel, and licorice, one qian each of angelica and white peony, one fen each of bupleurum and haritaki, along with three fen of cinnamon twig, seven fen of ephedra root, a pinch of floating wheat, and three fen of processed aconite. After three doses, the sweating stopped, the fever retreated, and he felt at ease.

    The "Medical Compendium" states: A man experienced sweating in his hands and feet, and despite the doctor's use of bitter herbs like coptis, scutellaria, and others in addition to tonics, there was no effect. His foot sweating was particularly excessive, so later, a prescription consisting of Eight Treasures, complemented by half of something and poria as the sovereign, along with white aconite and chuanwu as aides, successfully eliminated the sweating.[82p]

    　　《薛己医案》曰：一儒者数勤苦，因饮食失节，大便下血，或赤或黯，半载之后，非便血则盗汗，非恶寒则发热，血汗二药，用之无效，六脉浮大，心脾则濇，此思伤心脾，不能摄血归源。然血即汗，汗即血，其色赤黯，便血盗汗，皆火之升降微甚耳。恶寒发热，气血俱虚也。乃午前用补中益气，以补脾肺之源，举下陷之气；午后用归脾加麦门五味，以补心脾之血，收耗散之液，不两月而诸证悉愈。
    　　下堡顾仁成年六十有一，痢后入房，精滑自遗，二日方止。又房劳感寒怒气，遂发寒热，右胁痛连心胸，腹痞，自汗盗汗如雨，四肢厥冷，睡中惊悸，或觉上升如浮，或觉下陷如堕，遂致废寝。或用补药二剂益甚，脉浮大洪数，按之微细，此属无火虚热，急与十全大补加山药、山茱、丹皮、附子一剂，诸证顿愈而痊。此等元气，百无一二。[83p]

    The "Case Studies of Xue Ji" states: A scholar exerted himself greatly, and due to irregularities in diet, experienced bloody stools, which were either red or dark. After half a year, if not blood in the stools, then there was night sweating; if not experiencing cold chills, then there was fever. The two treatments of blood and sweat had no effect; the six pulses were floating and large, while the heart and spleen were depleted. This resulted from overthinking, which harmed the heart and spleen, causing an inability to contain blood and restore it to its source. However, blood is indeed sweat, and sweat is blood; their colors, red and dark, indicate minor or severe fluctuations of fire. Chills and fever indicated a deficiency of both qi and blood. Thus, in the morning, I employed a restorative formula to tonify the middle and augment qi, aiming to strengthen the source of the spleen and lungs and lift the sinking qi; in the afternoon, I used Gui Pi (Return the Spleen) with black and five flavors, to nourish the blood of the heart and spleen, consolidating the dispersed fluids. Within two months, all symptoms completely resolved.

    Xia Bao Gu Ren, aged sixty-one, after suffering from dysentery, experienced involuntary semen leakage for two days before it ceased. Moreover, after exertions in intimacy, he caught a chill and became angry, which led to the onset of chills and fever, pain in the right side radiating to the chest, abdominal distension, spontaneous sweating, and night sweats like rain, with his limbs feeling cold and experiencing frightful waking moments, sometimes feeling as though rising like floating or sinking like falling, which led to insomnia. Using two doses of tonifying medicine further aggravated the condition; his pulse was floating, large, and rapid, but when examined, it was weak and thin. This indicated a fire-less, deficient heat, so I urgently prescribed a formula of Ten Complete Powders, adding dioscorea, dogwood, peony, and prepared aconite, after which all symptoms suddenly improved and he was restored to health. Such vitality is exceptionally rare.[83p]

    　　一儒者口干发热，小便频浊，大便秘结，盗汗梦遗，遂致废寝，用当归六黄汤二剂，盗汗顿止；用六味地黄丸，二便调和；用十全大补汤及前丸，兼服月余而悉愈。
    　　《景岳全书》曰：余尝治一衰翁，年逾七旬，陡患伤寒，初起即用温补调理，至十日之外，正气将复，忽尔作战，自旦至辰，不能得汗，寒栗危甚，告急于余。余用六味回阳饮入人参一两、姜附各三钱，使之煎服，下咽少顷，即大汗如浴，时将及午而浸汗不收，身冷如脱，鼻息几无，复以告余。余令以前药复煎与之，告者曰：先服此药，已大汗不堪，今又服此，尚堪再汗乎？余笑谓曰：此中有神，非尔所知也。急令再进，遂汗收神复，不旬日而起矣。呜呼！发汗用此，而收汗复用此，无怪乎人之疑之也。而不知汗之出与汗之收，皆元气为之枢机耳。故余纪此，欲人知阖辟之权，不在乎能放能收，而在乎所以主之者。
    [84p]

    A scholar suffered from a dry mouth and fever, frequent and turbid urination, constipation, nocturnal sweating, and nocturnal emissions, which led to insomnia. I prescribed two doses of Danggui Liuhuang Decoction, and the nocturnal sweating immediately stopped. I then used Liuwei Dihuang Pill to regulate his urination and bowel movements. After taking a decoction of Shiquan Dabu Decoction along with the previous pill for over a month, he was completely cured.

    In the "Complete Book of Jingyue," it says: I once treated an elderly man over seventy who suddenly suffered from a cold infection. Initially, I used warming and tonifying methods. After ten days, when his vital energy was about to recover, he unexpectedly had a gastrointestinal crisis—fighting violently from dawn until 9 AM without being able to sweat, experiencing severe chills and danger, and urgently called for me. I administered Liuwei Huayang Decoction with one tael of ginseng and three qian each of ginger and aconite, making him take it as a brew. After a brief time, he broke out in sweat, as if bathed. By noon, he was drenched in sweat and could hardly recover, feeling cold as if he were dead, with almost no breath. I was informed of this again. I commanded that the previous medicine be brewed again for him, but the messenger said: "He has already sweated profusely from this medicine; can he endure more sweating with another dose?" I laughed and said: "There is a principle in this that you do not understand." I insisted on administering it again, and this led to the cessation of sweating and the recovery of his spirit. Within a few days, he was up and about. Alas! Using this method to induce sweating and to subsequently stop sweating may lead people to doubt its efficacy. However, they do not realize that both the emergence and cessation of sweat are controlled by the vital energy. Therefore, I record this to allow people to understand that the power of contraction and expansion does not lie merely in the ability to release or retrieve but in what governs it.[84p]
